(2,850/sq&#160;mi)</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row">&#160;•&#160;Major Ethnolinguistic Groups<div style="font-weight:normal;display:inline;"></div></th><td><a href="#cite_note-snhdi-gdl-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> (<span style="color:#fc0">medium</span>) · <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_states_and_territories_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of Indian states and territories by Human Development Index">29th</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Literacy_in_India" title="Literacy in India">Literacy</a> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047488"/><span class="nobold">(2011)</span></th><td>63.82%<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011Literacy_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011Literacy-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Human_sex_ratio" title="Human sex ratio">Sex ratio</a> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047488"/><span class="nobold">(2011)</span></th><td>918 <a href="/wiki/Females" class="mw-redirect" title="Females">♀</a>/1000 <a href="/wiki/Males" class="mw-redirect" title="Males">♂</a><sup id="cite_ref-pc-census2011_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pc-census2011-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://gov.bih.nic.in/">gov<wbr />.bih<wbr />.nic<wbr />.in</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Bihar</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;h&#39; in &#39;hi&#39;">h</span><span title="/ɑːr/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;far&#39;">ɑːr</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>Hindi pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Hindi_and_Urdu" title="Help:IPA/Hindi and Urdu">[bɪˈɦaːr]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bihar.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a2/Bihar.ogg" class="internal" title="Bihar.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>) is a <a href="/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India" title="States and union territories of India">state</a> in eastern <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_and_union_territories_of_India_by_area" title="List of states and union territories of India by area">twelfth-largest Indian state</a>, with an area of 94,163&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (36,357&#160;sq&#160;mi). The <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_and_union_territories_of_India_by_population" title="List of states and union territories of India by population">third-largest state by population</a>, it is contiguous with <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a> to its west, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> to the north, the northern part of <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a> to the east, with <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a> to the south. The Bihar plain is split by the river <a href="/wiki/Ganges" title="Ganges">Ganges</a>, which flows from west to east.<sup id="cite_ref-GovBiharProfile_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GovBiharProfile-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Three main regions converge in the state: <a href="/wiki/Magadh" class="mw-redirect" title="Magadh">Magadh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mithila_(region)" title="Mithila (region)">Mithila</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_region" title="Bhojpuri region">Bhojpur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 November 2000, southern Bihar was ceded to form the new state of <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Only 11.3% of the population of Bihar lives in urban areas, which is the lowest in India after <a href="/wiki/Himachal_Pradesh" title="Himachal Pradesh">Himachal Pradesh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, almost 58% of <a href="/wiki/Bihari_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bihari people">Biharis</a> are below the age of 25, giving Bihar the highest proportion of young people of any Indian state.<sup id="cite_ref-economic_strangulation_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economic_strangulation-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In ancient and classical India, the area that is now Bihar was considered a centre of power, learning, and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> From Magadha arose India's first empire, the <a href="/wiki/Maurya_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Maurya empire">Maurya empire</a>, as well as one of the world's most widely adhered-to religions, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Magadha empires, notably under the <a href="/wiki/Maurya" class="mw-redirect" title="Maurya">Maurya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gupta_Empire" title="Gupta Empire">Gupta</a> dynasties, unified large parts of South Asia under a central rule.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Another region of Bihar is <a href="/wiki/Mithila_(region)" title="Mithila (region)">Mithila</a> which was an early centre of Vedic learning and the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Videha" class="mw-redirect" title="Videha">Videha</a> kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the late 1970s, Bihar has lagged far behind other Indian states in terms of social and economic development.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Many economists and social scientists claim that this is a direct result of the policies of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">central government</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Freight_equalisation_policy" title="Freight equalisation policy">freight equalization policy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-saibal_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saibal-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> its apathy towards Bihar,<sup id="cite_ref-economic_strangulation_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economic_strangulation-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CPASGuruswamy20040615_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPASGuruswamy20040615-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CPASGuruswamy20040215_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPASGuruswamy20040215-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> lack of Bihari sub-nationalism,<sup id="cite_ref-saibal_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saibal-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Settlement" title="Permanent Settlement">Permanent Settlement</a> of 1793 by the <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">British East India Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-saibal_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saibal-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The state government has, however, made significant strides in developing the state.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Improved governance has led to an economic revival in the state through increased investment in infrastructure,<sup id="cite_ref-bihar_basher_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bihar_basher-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> better health care facilities, greater emphasis on education, and a reduction in crime and corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>The name <i>Bihar</i> is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pali" title="Pali">Pali</a> word <i><a href="/wiki/Vih%C4%81ra" class="mw-redirect" title="Vihāra">vihāra</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Devanagari" title="Devanagari">Devanagari</a>: विहार), meaning "abode". The region roughly encompassing the present state was dotted with Buddhist viharas, the abodes of Buddhist monks in the ancient and medieval periods. Medieval writer <a href="/wiki/Minhaj_al-Siraj_Juzjani" class="mw-redirect" title="Minhaj al-Siraj Juzjani">Minhaj al-Siraj Juzjani</a> records in the <i><a href="/wiki/Tabaqat-i_Nasiri" title="Tabaqat-i Nasiri">Tabaqat-i Nasiri</a></i> that in 1198 <a href="/wiki/Ikhtiyar_Uddin_Muhammad_bin_Bakhtiyar_Khilji" class="mw-redirect" title="Ikhtiyar Uddin Muhammad bin Bakhtiyar Khilji">Bakhtiyar Khalji</a> committed a massacre in a town identified with the word, later known as <a href="/wiki/Bihar_Sharif" title="Bihar Sharif">Bihar Sharif</a>, about 70&#160;km away from <a href="/wiki/Bodh_Gaya" title="Bodh Gaya">Bodh Gaya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bihar" title="History of Bihar">History of Bihar</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_for_Bihar" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline for Bihar">Timeline for Bihar</a>; <a href="/wiki/Magadha" title="Magadha">Magadha</a>; <a href="/wiki/Mithila_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Mithila Kingdom">Mithila Kingdom</a>; <a href="/wiki/History_of_Buddhism_in_India" title="History of Buddhism in India">History of Buddhism in India</a>; <a href="/wiki/Decline_of_Buddhism_in_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Decline of Buddhism in India">Decline of Buddhism in India</a>; <a href="/wiki/Mithila,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Mithila, India">Mithila, India</a>; and <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Mithila" class="mw-redirect" title="List of rulers of Mithila">List of rulers of Mithila</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_period">Ancient period</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:240px;max-width:240px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:264px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Kundpur_seal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Kundpur_seal.jpg/238px-Kundpur_seal.jpg" decoding="async" width="238" height="265" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Kundpur_seal.jpg/357px-Kundpur_seal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Kundpur_seal.jpg/476px-Kundpur_seal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="780" data-file-height="867" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">Copy of the seal excavated from Kundpur, <a href="/wiki/Vaishali_(ancient_city)" title="Vaishali (ancient city)">Vaishali</a>. The Brahmi letters on the seal state: "Kundpur was in Vaishali. Prince Vardhaman (<a href="/wiki/Mahavira" title="Mahavira">Mahavira</a>) used this seal after the <i>Judgement</i>."</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:240px;max-width:240px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:176px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Mahajanapadas_(c._500_BCE).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png/238px-Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png" decoding="async" width="238" height="176" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png/357px-Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png/476px-Mahajanapadas_%28c._500_BCE%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="889" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center"><a href="/wiki/Magadha" title="Magadha">Magadha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anga" title="Anga">Anga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vajji" title="Vajji">Vajjian</a> Confederacy of Mithila in <i>circa</i> 600&#160;BCE.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chirand" title="Chirand">Chirand</a>, on the northern bank of the <a href="/wiki/Ganga_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ganga River">Ganga River</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Saran_district" title="Saran district">Saran district</a>, has an archaeological record from the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Neolithic age">Neolithic age</a> (about 2500–1345 BC).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Regions of Bihar—such as <a href="/wiki/Magadha" title="Magadha">Magadha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mithila_(region)" title="Mithila (region)">Mithila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anga" title="Anga">Anga</a>—are mentioned in religious texts and epics of ancient India.
</p><p>Mithila gained prominence after the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Videha" class="mw-redirect" title="Videha">Videha</a> Kingdom<sup id="cite_ref-gov.bih.nic.in_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov.bih.nic.in-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient India">ancient India</a>. During the late Vedic period (c. 1100-500 BCE), Videha became one of the major political and cultural centers of South Asia, along with Kuru and Pañcāla. The kings of the Videha Kingdom were called <a href="/wiki/Janaka" title="Janaka">Janakas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sita" title="Sita">Sita</a>, a daughter of one of the Janaks of <a href="/wiki/Mithila,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Mithila, India">Mithila</a> is mentioned as the consort of <a href="/wiki/Rama" title="Rama">Lord Rama</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_epic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu epic">Hindu epic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a>, written by <a href="/wiki/Valmiki" title="Valmiki">Valmiki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gov.bih.nic.in_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov.bih.nic.in-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (January 2019)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The Videha Kingdom later became incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Vajji" title="Vajji">Vajji</a> confederacy which had its capital in the city of <a href="/wiki/Vaishali_(ancient_city)" title="Vaishali (ancient city)">Vaishali</a>, which is also in Mithila.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Vajji had a republican form of government where the king was elected from the number of rajas. Based on the information found in texts pertaining to Jainism and Buddhism, Vajji was established as a republic by the 6th century BCE, before the birth of <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">Gautama Buddha</a> in 563 BCE, making it the first known republic in India.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Haryanka_dynasty" title="Haryanka dynasty">Haryanka dynasty</a>, founded in 684 BC, ruled Magadha from the city of <a href="/wiki/Rajgriha" class="mw-redirect" title="Rajgriha">Rajgriha</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Rajgir" title="Rajgir">Rajgir</a>). The two well-known kings from this dynasty were <a href="/wiki/Bimbisara" title="Bimbisara">Bimbisara</a> and his son <a href="/wiki/Ajatashatru" title="Ajatashatru">Ajatashatru</a>, who imprisoned his father to ascend the throne. Ajatashatru founded the city of <a href="/wiki/Pataliputra" title="Pataliputra">Pataliputra</a> which later became the capital of Magadha. He declared war and conquered the <a href="/wiki/Vajji" title="Vajji">Vajji</a>. The Haryanka dynasty was followed by the <a href="/wiki/Shishunaga_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Shishunaga dynasty">Shishunaga dynasty</a>. Later the <a href="/wiki/Nanda_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Nanda Dynasty">Nanda Dynasty</a> ruled a vast tract stretching from <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a> to <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_India" title="Punjab, India">Punjab</a>.
</p><p>The Nanda dynasty was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Maurya_Empire" title="Maurya Empire">Maurya Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>'s first empire. The Maurya Empire and the religion of <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> arose in the region that now makes up modern Bihar. The Mauryan Empire, which originated from Magadha in 325 BC, was founded by <a href="/wiki/Chandragupta_Maurya" title="Chandragupta Maurya">Chandragupta Maurya</a>, who was born in Magadha. It had its capital at <a href="/wiki/Pataliputra" title="Pataliputra">Pataliputra</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Mauryan" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauryan">Mauryan</a> emperor, <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">Ashoka</a>, who was born in Pataliputra (Patna) is believed to be one of the greatest rulers in the history of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Gupta Empire, which originated in Magadha in 240 AD, is referred as the Golden Age of India in science, mathematics, astronomy, commerce, religion, and <a href="/wiki/Indian_philosophy" title="Indian philosophy">Indian philosophy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Bihar and Bengal was invaded by <a href="/wiki/Rajendra_Chola_I" title="Rajendra Chola I">Rajendra Chola I</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Chola_dynasty" title="Chola dynasty">Chola dynasty</a> in the 11th century.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_period">Medieval period</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ravi_Varma-Shakuntala_columbia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="It is one of the legacies of the Gupta Empire" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ravi_Varma-Shakuntala_columbia.jpg/150px-Ravi_Varma-Shakuntala_columbia.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ravi_Varma-Shakuntala_columbia.jpg/225px-Ravi_Varma-Shakuntala_columbia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Ravi_Varma-Shakuntala_columbia.jpg/300px-Ravi_Varma-Shakuntala_columbia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="544" data-file-height="803" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ravi_Varma-Shakuntala_columbia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kalidasa" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalidasa">Kalidasa</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> play <i><a href="/wiki/Abhij%C3%B1%C4%81na%C5%9B%C4%81kuntalam" class="mw-redirect" title="Abhijñānaśākuntalam">Abhijñānaśākuntalam</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>Buddhism in Magadha went into decline due to the invasion of <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_bin_Bakhtiyar_Khalji" title="Muhammad bin Bakhtiyar Khalji">Muhammad bin Bakhtiyar Khalji</a>, during which many of the <a href="/wiki/Viharas" class="mw-redirect" title="Viharas">viharas</a> and the famed universities of <a href="/wiki/Nalanda" title="Nalanda">Nalanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vikramashila" title="Vikramashila">Vikramashila</a> were destroyed. It was claimed that thousands of <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> monks were massacred during the 12th century.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> D. N. Jha suggests, instead, that these incidents were the result of Buddhist-Brahmin skirmishes in a fight for supremacy.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> After the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Pala_Empire" title="Pala Empire">Pala Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chero_dynasty" title="Chero dynasty">Chero dynasty</a> ruled some parts of Bihar from the 12th century to the 16th century until <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal rule</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In 1540, the great <a href="/wiki/Pashtun_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Pashtun people">Pathan</a> chieftain, <a href="/wiki/Sher_Shah_Suri" title="Sher Shah Suri">Sher Shah Suri</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Sasaram" title="Sasaram">Sasaram</a>, took northern India from the Mughals, defeating the Mughal army of Emperor Humayun. Sher Shah declared Delhi his capital.
</p><p>From the 11th century to the 20th century, Mithila was ruled by various indigenous dynasties. The first of these were the <a href="/wiki/Karnatas_of_Mithila" class="mw-redirect" title="Karnatas of Mithila">Karnatas</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Oiniwar_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Oiniwar dynasty">Oiniwar dynasty</a> and finally <a href="/wiki/Raj_Darbhanga" title="Raj Darbhanga">Raj Darbhanga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
It was during this period that the capital of Mithila was shifted to <a href="/wiki/Darbhanga" title="Darbhanga">Darbhanga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The tenth and the last <i><a href="/wiki/Sikh_gurus" title="Sikh gurus">Guru</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guru_Gobind_Singh" title="Guru Gobind Singh">Guru Gobind Singh</a> was born in Patna.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_Era">Colonial Era</span></h3>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Buxar" title="Battle of Buxar">Battle of Buxar</a> (1764), the <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">British East India Company</a> obtained the diwani rights (rights to administer, and collect revenue or tax) for Bihar, <a href="/wiki/Bengal" title="Bengal">Bengal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">Odisha</a>. The rich resources of fertile land, water and skilled labour had attracted the foreign imperialists, particularly the Dutch and British, in the 18th century. A number of agriculture-based industries had been started in Bihar by foreign entrepreneurs.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Bihar remained a part of the <a href="/wiki/Bengal_Presidency" title="Bengal Presidency">Bengal Presidency</a> of <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British India</a> until 1912, when the province of <a href="/wiki/Bihar_and_Orissa" class="mw-redirect" title="Bihar and Orissa">Bihar and Orissa</a> was carved out as a separate province. Since 2010, Bihar has celebrated its birthday as <a href="/wiki/Bihar_Sthapana_Diwas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bihar Sthapana Diwas">Bihar Diwas</a> on 22 March.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-_and_post-Independence">Pre- and post-Independence</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dr_Rajendra_Pd._DR.Anugrah_Narayan_Sinha.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Dr_Rajendra_Pd._DR.Anugrah_Narayan_Sinha.jpg/200px-Dr_Rajendra_Pd._DR.Anugrah_Narayan_Sinha.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="304" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Dr_Rajendra_Pd._DR.Anugrah_Narayan_Sinha.jpg/300px-Dr_Rajendra_Pd._DR.Anugrah_Narayan_Sinha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Dr_Rajendra_Pd._DR.Anugrah_Narayan_Sinha.jpg/400px-Dr_Rajendra_Pd._DR.Anugrah_Narayan_Sinha.jpg 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="957" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dr_Rajendra_Pd._DR.Anugrah_Narayan_Sinha.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>(Sitting L to R): Rajendra Prasad and Anugrah Narayan Sinha during <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a>'s 1917 Champaran Satyagraha</div></div></div>
<p>Farmers in <a href="/wiki/Champaran" title="Champaran">Champaran</a> had revolted against <a href="/wiki/Indigo" title="Indigo">indigo</a> cultivation in 1914 (at <a href="/wiki/Pipra" title="Pipra">Pipra</a>) and 1916 (Turkaulia). In April 1917, <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a> visited Champaran, where <a href="/wiki/Raj_Kumar_Shukla" title="Raj Kumar Shukla">Raj Kumar Shukla</a> had drawn his attention to the exploitation of the peasants by European <a href="/wiki/Indigo" title="Indigo">indigo</a> planters. The <a href="/wiki/Champaran_Satyagraha" title="Champaran Satyagraha">Champaran Satyagraha</a> that followed received support from many Bihari nationalists, such as <a href="/wiki/Rajendra_Prasad" title="Rajendra Prasad">Rajendra Prasad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anugrah_Narayan_Sinha" title="Anugrah Narayan Sinha">Anugrah Narayan Sinha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the northern and central regions of Bihar, the <a href="/wiki/All_India_Kisan_Sabha" title="All India Kisan Sabha">Kisan Sabha</a> (<a href="/wiki/Peasant" title="Peasant">peasant</a> movement) was an important consequence of the independence movement. It began in 1929 under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Swami_Sahajanand_Saraswati" class="mw-redirect" title="Swami Sahajanand Saraswati">Swami Sahajanand Saraswati</a> who formed the <a href="/wiki/Bihar_Provincial_Kisan_Sabha" class="mw-redirect" title="Bihar Provincial Kisan Sabha">Bihar Provincial Kisan Sabha</a> (BPKS), to mobilise peasant grievances against the <a href="/wiki/Zamindari" class="mw-redirect" title="Zamindari">zamindari</a> attacks on their occupancy rights. The movement intensified and spread from Bihar across the rest of India, culminating in the formation of the <a href="/wiki/All_India_Kisan_Sabha" title="All India Kisan Sabha">All India Kisan Sabha</a> (AIKS) at the <a href="/wiki/Lucknow" title="Lucknow">Lucknow</a> session of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a> in April 1936, where Saraswati was elected as its first president.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bihari_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bihari people">Bihari</a> migrant workers have faced violence and prejudice in many parts of India, such as <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_India" title="Punjab, India">Punjab</a> and <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a> after independence.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/2008_attacks_on_North_Indians_in_Maharashtra" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 attacks on North Indians in Maharashtra">2008 attacks on North Indians in Maharashtra</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Bihar" title="Geography of Bihar">Geography of Bihar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Bihar" title="Climate of Bihar">Climate of Bihar</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Biharimap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Biharimap.png/230px-Biharimap.png" decoding="async" width="230" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Biharimap.png/345px-Biharimap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Biharimap.png/460px-Biharimap.png 2x" data-file-width="752" data-file-height="473" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Biharimap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>River Map of Bihar</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mountain_of_Ashram.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Mountain_of_Ashram.jpg/170px-Mountain_of_Ashram.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Mountain_of_Ashram.jpg/255px-Mountain_of_Ashram.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Mountain_of_Ashram.jpg/340px-Mountain_of_Ashram.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1840" data-file-height="1232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mountain_of_Ashram.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mountain of <a href="/wiki/Ashram" title="Ashram">Ashrams</a>, near Sena Village, at <a href="/wiki/Buddha_Gaya" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddha Gaya">Buddha Gaya</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flooded_Bihar.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flooded_Bihar.JPG/170px-Flooded_Bihar.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flooded_Bihar.JPG/255px-Flooded_Bihar.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Flooded_Bihar.JPG/340px-Flooded_Bihar.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flooded_Bihar.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flooded farmlands in northern Bihar during the <a href="/wiki/2008_Bihar_flood" title="2008 Bihar flood">2008 Bihar flood</a></div></div></div>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Climate_of_India" title="Climate of India">Climate</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Classification</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/Climatic_regions_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Climatic regions of India">Cwa</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Avg. temperature</th><td>27&#160;°C (81&#160;°F)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">• Summer</th><td>34&#160;°C (93&#160;°F)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">• Winter</th><td>10&#160;°C (50&#160;°F)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a></th><td>1,200&#160;mm (47&#160;in)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Bihar has a diverse climate. Its temperature is subtropical in general, with hot summers and cold winters. Bihar is a vast stretch of fertile plain. It is drained by the <a href="/wiki/Ganges" title="Ganges">Ganges</a> River, including its northern tributaries <a href="/wiki/Gandaki_River" title="Gandaki River">Gandak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Koshi_River" title="Koshi River">Koshi</a>, originating in the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Nepal" title="Geography of Nepal">Nepal</a> <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bagmati" class="mw-redirect" title="Bagmati">Bagmati</a> originating in the <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_Valley" title="Kathmandu Valley">Kathmandu Valley</a> that regularly <a href="/wiki/2008_Bihar_flood" title="2008 Bihar flood">flood</a> parts of the Bihar plains. The total area covered by the state of Bihar is 94,163&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (36,357&#160;sq&#160;mi). the state is located between 24°-20'-10" N ~ 27°-31'-15" N latitude and between 83°-19'-50" E ~ 88°-17'-40" E longitude. Its average elevation above sea level is 173 feet (53&#160;m).
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ganges" title="Ganges">Ganges</a> divides Bihar into two unequal halves and flows through the middle from west to east. Other Ganges tributaries are the Son, <a href="/wiki/Budhi_Gandak" class="mw-redirect" title="Budhi Gandak">Budhi Gandak</a>, Chandan, Orhani and <a href="/wiki/Phalgu" title="Phalgu">Phalgu</a>. Though the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a> begin at the <a href="/wiki/Siwaliks" class="mw-redirect" title="Siwaliks">foothills</a>, a short distance inside <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> and to the north of Bihar, the mountains influence Bihar's landforms, climate, hydrology and culture. Central parts of Bihar have some small hills, for example, the <a href="/wiki/Rajgir_hills" title="Rajgir hills">Rajgir hills</a>. To the south is the Chota Nagpur plateau, which was part of Bihar until 2000 but now is part of a separate state called <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bauhinia_Acuminata.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Bauhinia_Acuminata.jpg/170px-Bauhinia_Acuminata.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Bauhinia_Acuminata.jpg/255px-Bauhinia_Acuminata.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Bauhinia_Acuminata.jpg/340px-Bauhinia_Acuminata.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bauhinia_Acuminata.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bauhinia_acuminata" title="Bauhinia acuminata">Bauhinia acuminata</a>, locally known as <i>Kachnaar</i></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Flora_of_Bihar" title="Flora of Bihar">Flora of Bihar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Bihar" title="Fauna of Bihar">Fauna of Bihar</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Bihar" title="Protected areas of Bihar">Protected areas of Bihar</a></div>
<p>Bihar has notified forest area of 6,845&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2,643&#160;sq&#160;mi), which is 7.27% of its geographical area.<sup id="cite_ref-Forest_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forest-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The sub Himalayan foothill of Someshwar and the Dun ranges in the Champaran district are another belt of moist deciduous forests. These also consist of shrubs, grass and reeds. Here the rainfall is above 1,600 millimetres (63&#160;in) and thus promotes luxuriant Sal forests in the area. The most important trees are <i><a href="/wiki/Shorea_robusta" title="Shorea robusta">Shorea Robusta</a></i>, Sal Cedrela Toona, <a href="/wiki/Khair" title="Khair">Khair</a>, and Semal. Deciduous forests also occur in the <a href="/wiki/Saharsa" title="Saharsa">Saharsa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Purnia" title="Purnia">Purnia</a> districts.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> <i>Shorea robusta</i> (sal), <a href="/wiki/Diospyros_melanoxylon" title="Diospyros melanoxylon">Diospyros melanoxylon</a> (kendu), <i><a href="/wiki/Boswellia_serrata" title="Boswellia serrata">Boswellia serrata</a></i> (salai), <i><a href="/wiki/Terminalia_elliptica" title="Terminalia elliptica">Terminalia tomentose</a></i> (asan), <i><a href="/wiki/Terminalia_bellirica" title="Terminalia bellirica">Terminalia bellerica</a></i> (bahera), <i><a href="/wiki/Terminalia_arjuna" title="Terminalia arjuna">Terminalia Arjuna</a></i> (arjun), <i><a href="/wiki/Pterocarpus_marsupium" title="Pterocarpus marsupium">Pterocarpus marsupium</a></i> (paisar), <i><a href="/wiki/Madhuca_indica" class="mw-redirect" title="Madhuca indica">Madhuca indica</a></i> (mahua) are the common <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">flora</a> across the forest of Bihar.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Valmiki_National_Park" title="Valmiki National Park">Valmiki National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Champaran_district" title="West Champaran district">West Champaran district</a>, covering about 800&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (309&#160;sq&#160;mi) of forest, is the 18th <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Reserve_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiger Reserve of India">Tiger Reserve of India</a> and is ranked fourth in terms of density of <a href="/wiki/Tiger" title="Tiger">tiger</a> population.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> It has a diverse landscape, sheltering rich wildlife habitats and floral and faunal composition, along with the prime protected carnivores. <a href="/wiki/Vikramshila_Gangetic_Dolphin_Sanctuary" title="Vikramshila Gangetic Dolphin Sanctuary">Vikramshila Gangetic Dolphin Sanctuary</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bhagalpur" title="Bhagalpur">Bhagalpur</a> region is a sanctuary of the endangered <a href="/wiki/Gangetic_dolphin" class="mw-redirect" title="Gangetic dolphin">Gangetic dolphin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Forest_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forest-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Other notable sanctuaries include <a href="/wiki/Kaimur_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Kaimur Wildlife Sanctuary">Kaimur Wildlife Sanctuary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhimbandh_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Bhimbandh Wildlife Sanctuary">Bhimbandh Wildlife Sanctuary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gautam_Buddha_Wildlife_Sanctuary" class="mw-redirect" title="Gautam Buddha Wildlife Sanctuary">Gautam Buddha Wildlife Sanctuary</a>.
</p><p>Other species include leopard, bear, hyena, bison, chital and <a href="/wiki/Barking_deer" class="mw-redirect" title="Barking deer">barking deer</a>. Crocodiles (including <a href="/wiki/Mugger_crocodile" title="Mugger crocodile">muggers</a>) and Gangetic turtles can be found in the river systems. Many varieties of local bird species as well as migratory birds can be seen in natural wetlands of <a href="/wiki/Kanwar_Lake_Bird_Sanctuary" title="Kanwar Lake Bird Sanctuary">Kanwar Lake Bird Sanctuary</a>, Baraila lake, Kusheshwar Nath Lake, Udaypur lake. Nagi Dam and Nakti Dam have been declared as bird sanctuary.<sup id="cite_ref-Forest_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forest-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Maithili_language" title="Maithili language">Maithili</a> (12.55%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a> (0.78%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:brown; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Santali_language" title="Santali language">Santali</a> (0.44%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:white; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other (0.29%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p>After the 2011 Census, Bihar was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_and_union_territories_of_India_by_population" title="List of states and union territories of India by population">third most populous</a> <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="States and territories of India">state of India</a> with total population of 104,099,452 (54,278,157 male and 49,821,295 female). Nearly 89% of Bihar's population lived in rural areas. The density was 1,106.  The <a href="/wiki/Human_sex_ratio" title="Human sex ratio">sex ratio</a> was 918 females per 1000 males.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Almost 58% of Bihar's population was below 25 years age, which is the highest in India. Most of Bihar's population belongs to Indo-Aryan-speaking ethnic groups along with few Dravidian-speaking and Austroasiatic-speaking people mostly in Chhotanagpur Plateau (now part of Jharkhand). It also attracted <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Punjabi people">Punjabi</a> Hindu refugees during the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">Partition of British India</a> in 1947.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Bihar has a total <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> of 63.82% (73.39% for males and 53.33% for females), recording a growth of 20% in female literacy over the period of a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011Literacy_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011Literacy-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At 11.3%, Bihar has the second lowest urbanisation rate in India.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> As of the 2011 census<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bihar&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, population density surpassed 1,000 per square kilometre, making Bihar India's most densely-populated state, but still lower than <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a> or <a href="/wiki/Banten" title="Banten">Banten</a> of <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>.
</p><p>According to the 2011 census, 82.7% of Bihar's population practised Hinduism, while 16.9% followed Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-census2011_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2011-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_administration">Government and administration</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Bihar" title="Government of Bihar">Government of Bihar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Administration_in_Bihar" title="Administration in Bihar">Administration in Bihar</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Divisions_of_Bihar" title="Divisions of Bihar">Divisions of Bihar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Bihar" class="mw-redirect" title="Districts of Bihar">Districts of Bihar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretariat_Building_patna.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Secretariat_Building_patna.JPG/220px-Secretariat_Building_patna.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Secretariat_Building_patna.JPG/330px-Secretariat_Building_patna.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Secretariat_Building_patna.JPG/440px-Secretariat_Building_patna.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1684" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretariat_Building_patna.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Patna_Secretariat" title="Patna Secretariat">Vidhansabha Building</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a></div></div></div>
<p>The constitutional head of the government of Bihar is the governor, who is appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_India" title="President of India">President of India</a>. The real executive power rests with the <a href="/wiki/Chief_minister" title="Chief minister">chief minister</a> and the cabinet. The political party or the coalition of political parties having a majority in the Legislative Assembly forms the government.
</p><p>The head of the bureaucracy of the state is the chief secretary. Under this position, is a hierarchy of officials drawn from the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Administrative_Service" title="Indian Administrative Service">Indian Administrative Service</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_Police_Service" title="Indian Police Service">Indian Police Service</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_Forest_Service" title="Indian Forest Service">Indian Forest Service</a>, and different wings of the state civil services. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is headed by the Chief Justice. Bihar has a <a href="/wiki/Patna_High_Court" title="Patna High Court">High Court</a> which has been functioning since 1916. All the branches of the government are located in the state capital, Patna.
</p><p>The state is divided into nine divisions and 38 districts, for administrative purposes. Bihar has 12 Municipal Corporations, 49 Nagar Parishads, and 80 Nagar Panchayats.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bihar" title="Politics of Bihar">Politics of Bihar</a></div>
<dl><dd><i>See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Political_parties_in_Bihar" title="Category:Political parties in Bihar">Political parties in Bihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Bihar" title="Elections in Bihar">Elections in Bihar</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_politicians_from_Bihar" title="List of politicians from Bihar">List of politicians from Bihar</a></i>; <a href="/wiki/2015_Bihar_Legislative_Assembly_election" title="2015 Bihar Legislative Assembly election">2015 Bihar Legislative Assembly election</a></dd></dl>
<p>By 2004, 14 years after <a href="/wiki/Lalu_Prasad_Yadav" title="Lalu Prasad Yadav">Lalu Prasad Yadav</a>'s victory, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> magazine said that "Bihar [had] become a byword for the worst of India, of widespread and inescapable poverty, of corrupt politicians indistinguishable from mafia-dons they patronise, caste-ridden social order that has retained the worst feudal cruelties".<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> believed that issues faced by the state were "enormous" because of "persistent poverty, complex social stratification, unsatisfactory infrastructure and weak governance".<sup id="cite_ref-wpbihar_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wpbihar-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
Currently, there are two main political formations: the <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Alliance_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Democratic Alliance (India)">National Democratic Alliance</a> (NDA) which comprises <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">Bharatiya Janata Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lok_Janashakti_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Lok Janashakti Party">Lok Janashakti Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rashtriya_Lok_Samta_Party" title="Rashtriya Lok Samta Party">Rashtriya Lok Samta Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_Awam_Morcha" title="Hindustani Awam Morcha">Hindustani Awam Morcha</a> and JD(U) (Joined recently after breaking the Grand Alliance with RJD and INC), Second is alliance between RJD and Indian National Congress. There are many other political formations. The <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_India" title="Communist Party of India">Communist Party of India</a> had a strong presence in Bihar at one time, but is weakened now.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The CPM and Forward Bloc have a minor presence, along with the other extreme Left.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In contrast to prior governments, which emphasized divisions of caste and religion, <a href="/wiki/Nitish_Kumar" title="Nitish Kumar">Nitish Kumar</a>'s manifesto was based on economic development, curbs on crime and corruption and greater social equality for all sections of society. Since 2010, the government has confiscated the properties of corrupt officials and redeployed them as schools buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Simultaneously they introduced Bihar Special Court Act to curb crime.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> It has also legislated for a two-hour break on Fridays, including lunch, to enable <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> employees to pray and thus cut down on post-lunch absenteeism by them.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The government has prohibited the sale and consumption of alcohol in the state since March 2016;<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> this ban has been linked to a drop in tourism to Bihar.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_Health">Public Health</span></h2>
<p>In Bihar, attempts have been made to establish a well-functioning department of public health. National efforts like the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Mission" title="National Health Mission">National Health Mission</a>, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://clinicalestablishments.gov.in/cms/Home.aspx">Clinical Establishments Act of 2010</a>, and the formation of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18093346">Empowered Action Group</a> (EAG) catalyze the disbursement of federal funds by expanding healthcare access and improving the quality of healthcare services to states in need. However, Bihar's ability to fully utilize this funding is lacking. Bihar's health care system has the appropriate policies in place to allow for the implementation of comprehensive healthcare treatment. However, it is in the execution and management of the funding and services where it falls behind. Overall, the lack of consistent monitoring tools for policy evaluation explain why a strategic, evidence based public health system has been slow to take root in the state of Bihar. Consequently, Bihar generally ranks weakest in health outcomes in comparison to other Indian states and even among its EAG counterparts.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Research indicates that Bihar relies on privatized hospitals to provide healthcare to the masses, it has high levels of unacknowledged corruption and also implements a vertical system of disease management. In fact, the ratio of private spending on health care relative to public spending in Bihar is the second highest in India.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> These factors have been found to be associated with slower healthcare delivery and a higher degree of economic burden as a consequence of steep healthcare costs.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Much of this is because Bihar lacks in the continuity and transparency of health reporting as required by the Clinical Establishments Act of 2010. In turn, this prevents the government from making evidence based conclusions about policy changes and hospital effectiveness. Rather, Bihar's health department displays patterns of ill-informed spending, inconsistent hiring, and erratic spending on healthcare infrastructure.
</p><p>For example, according to the Government of India's "Ministry of Health &amp; Family Welfare Health and Family Welfare Census Data 2008-2015",<sup id="cite_ref-:2_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> the number of healthcare professionals including registered nurses, auxiliary nurses, physicians and health supervisors at each hospital in Bihar have remained significantly lower compared to those working in Kerala, and do not seem to follow any sort of pattern. Rather, its number of registered healthcare professionals remains constant over time. Compared to Bihar, we see that Kerala's number of registered healthcare professionals consistently increase over time. According to “Rural Health Statistics 2015”, the greatest shortfalls exist among physicians and specialists across the state at least 75%.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> This extends to the number of actual health centers across Bihar as well, as it only has 50% of the sub-health centers, 60% of the primary health centers, and a mere 9% of the community health centers it needs based on the national government's supply to population norms. At a closer look, the number of hospital beds that Bihar includes in each government-run hospital actually decreased between 2008 and 2015, compared to the consistently increasing number of hospital beds in government-run Kerala hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Given the population of Bihar (population: 99 million) is much denser than Kerala (population: 35 million), these numbers suggest that Bihar is significantly behind in the number of healthcare professionals that should be employed within the state.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_95-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> It is likely that because there is a lack of data reporting, analysis and evaluation within Bihar that these trends exist.
</p><p>Despite these shortcomings, Bihar has shown gradual signs of public health improvement in a few areas. There is indeed a shortage of skilled healthcare professionals, but Bihar still benefits from a surplus of female health workers compared to male health workers.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_89-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> In terms of key impact indicators, between 2010 and 2013, the crude birth rate decreased by 2.3%, crude death rate decreased by 5.6%, infant mortality rate decreased by 12.7%, neo-natal mortality rate decreased by 8.6%, under 5 mortality rate decreased by 9.1%, and maternal mortality ratio decreased by 10.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_89-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It would suit Bihar well to continue to adapt common cost effective practices to strengthen their health systems data measurement and research.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Research has shown that the implementation of patient and caregiver surveys, exit interviews at health centers, vignettes, and audit studies are simple methods of bolstering reporting and evaluation in lower income areas such as Bihar.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bihar_Village_Bazaar.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Bihar_Village_Bazaar.JPG/180px-Bihar_Village_Bazaar.JPG" decoding="async" width="180" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Bihar_Village_Bazaar.JPG/270px-Bihar_Village_Bazaar.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Bihar_Village_Bazaar.JPG/360px-Bihar_Village_Bazaar.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="552" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bihar_Village_Bazaar.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A village market</div></div></div>
<p>Gross state domestic product of Bihar for the year 2013/2014 has been around 3683.37&#160;billion INR. By sectors, its composition is:
</p>
<dl><dd>Agriculture = 22%</dd>
<dd>Industry = 5%</dd>
<dd>Services = 73%.</dd></dl>
<p>Bihar is the fastest growing state in terms of gross state domestic product (GSDP), clocking a growth rate of 17.06% in FY 2014–15.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The economy of Bihar was projected to grow at a compound annual growth rate (CAGR) of 13.4% during 2012–2017, i.e. the 12th Five-Year Plan. Bihar has witnessed strong growth in per capita net state domestic product (NSDP). At current prices, per capita NSDP of the state grew at a CAGR of 12.91 per cent during 2004–05 to 2014–15.<sup id="cite_ref-ibef.org_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibef.org-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Bihar's per capita income went up by 40.6 per cent in the financial year 2014–15.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>
<p>Bihar is the fourth-largest producer of vegetables and the eighth-largest producer of fruits in India. Bihar has high agricultural production making it one of the strongest sectors of the state. About 80 percent of the state's population is employed in agriculture, which is higher as compared to India's average.<sup id="cite_ref-ibef.org_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibef.org-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The main agricultural products produced in Bihar are litchi, guava, mango, pineapple, brinjal, lady's finger, cauliflower, cabbage, rice, wheat and sugarcane, and sunflower. Though good soil and favourable climatic conditions such as good rainfall favour agriculture, it has to encounter flood threat as well, which may drain off the fertile soil, if not conserved properly.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The state (mostly southern parts) faces droughts almost every year affecting production of crops such as paddy.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span></h3>
<p>Prior to <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_prohibition_in_India#Bihar" title="Alcohol prohibition in India">prohibition</a>, Bihar emerged as a brewery hub with major domestic and foreign firms setting up production units in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> In August 2018, <a href="/wiki/United_Breweries_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="United Breweries Limited">United Breweries Limited</a> announced it would begin production of non-alcoholic beer at its previously defunct brewery in Bihar.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hajipur" title="Hajipur">Hajipur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalmianagar" title="Dalmianagar">Dalmianagar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barauni" title="Barauni">Barauni</a> are the major industrial city in  Bihar<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The state's debt was estimated at 77% of GDP by 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The Finance Ministry has given top priority to create investment opportunities for big industrial houses like <a href="/wiki/Reliance_Industries" class="mw-redirect" title="Reliance Industries">Reliance Industries</a>. Further developments have taken place in the growth of small industries, improvements in IT infrastructure, the new software park in Patna, Darbhanga, Bhagalpur<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> and the completion of the expressway from the Purvanchal border through Bihar to Jharkhand. In August 2008, a Patna registered company called the Security and Intelligence Services (SIS) India Limited<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> took over the Australian guard and mobile patrol services business of American conglomerate, <a href="/wiki/United_Technologies_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="United Technologies Corporation">United Technologies Corporation</a> (UTC). SIS is registered and taxed in Bihar.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The capital city, Patna, is one of the better-off cities in India when measured by per capita income.<sup id="cite_ref-patna_prosperity_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patna_prosperity-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1"><b><a href="#ref_1">^</a></b></span> 
The State Government is setting up an Information Technology (IT) City at <a href="/wiki/Rajgir" title="Rajgir">Rajgir</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nalanda_district" title="Nalanda district">Nalanda district</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, India's first Media Hub is also proposed to be set up in Bihar.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Income_distribution">Income distribution</span></h3>
<p>In terms of income, the districts of <a href="/wiki/Patna_district" title="Patna district">Patna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munger_district" title="Munger district">Munger</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Begusarai_district" title="Begusarai district">Begusarai</a> were the three best-off out of a total of 38 districts in the state, recording the highest per capita gross district <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">domestic product</a> of <span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>31,441, <span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>10,087 and <span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>9,312, respectively, in 2004–05.<sup id="cite_ref-patna_prosperity_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patna_prosperity-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bihar" class="mw-redirect" title="Culture of Bihar">Culture of Bihar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paag-mithila5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Paag-mithila5.jpg/220px-Paag-mithila5.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Paag-mithila5.jpg/330px-Paag-mithila5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Paag-mithila5.jpg/440px-Paag-mithila5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paag-mithila5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Paag" title="Paag">Paag</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mithila_(region)" title="Mithila (region)">Mithila</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language_and_literature">Language and literature</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Languages_in_Bihar" class="mw-redirect" title="Languages in Bihar">Languages in Bihar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Literature_in_Bihar" class="mw-redirect" title="Literature in Bihar">Literature in Bihar</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Maithili_language" title="Maithili language">Maithili language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhojpuri">Bhojpuri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angika" title="Angika">Angika</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magahi" class="mw-redirect" title="Magahi">Magahi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magadhi_Prakrit" title="Magadhi Prakrit">Magadhi Prakrit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindi_in_Bihar" title="Hindi in Bihar">Hindi in Bihar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Urdu_Language_in_Bihar" class="mw-redirect" title="Urdu Language in Bihar">Urdu Language in Bihar</a></div>

Tirhuta and Devanagari scripts</div></div></div> <p><a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> is the official language of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-CSDOffLang1950_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSDOffLang1950-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Urdu is the second official language in 15 districts of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-Benedikter2009_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benedikter2009-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maithili_language" title="Maithili language">Maithili</a> (including its dialect <a href="/wiki/Bajjika" title="Bajjika">Bajjika</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhojpuri">Bhojpuri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angika" title="Angika">Angika</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magahi" India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mha.nic.in_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mha.nic.in-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Proponents are calling for <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhojpuri">Bhojpuri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magahi" class="mw-redirect" title="Magahi">Magahi</a> to receive the same status.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paintings">Paintings</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mithila_painting" class="mw-redirect" title="Mithila painting">Mithila painting</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Madhubani_Mahavidyas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Madhubani_Mahavidyas.jpg/200px-Madhubani_Mahavidyas.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Madhubani_Mahavidyas.jpg/300px-Madhubani_Mahavidyas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Madhubani_Mahavidyas.jpg/400px-Madhubani_Mahavidyas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="623" data-file-height="850" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Madhubani_Mahavidyas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mithila Painting is also known as Madhubani art is a distinct type of painting style hailing from Mithila region of Bihar</div></div></div>
<p>There are several traditional styles of painting practiced in Bihar. One is <a href="/wiki/Mithila_painting" class="mw-redirect" title="Mithila painting">Mithila painting</a>, a style of Indian painting used in the <a href="/wiki/Mithila_(region)" title="Mithila (region)">Mithila</a> region of Bihar. Traditionally, the painting was one of the skills that was passed down from generation to generation in the families of the <a href="/wiki/Mithila_(region)" title="Mithila (region)">Mithila region</a>, mainly by women. Painting was usually done on walls during festivals, religious events, and other milestones of the life cycle, like birth, <a href="/wiki/Upanayanam" class="mw-redirect" title="Upanayanam">Upanayanam</a> (the sacred thread ceremony), and marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-Carolyn_Brown_Heinz_2006,_pp._5-33_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carolyn_Brown_Heinz_2006,_pp._5-33-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mithila painting was traditionally done on huts' freshly plastered mud walls, but today it is also done on cloth, handmade paper, and canvas. Famous Mithila painters have included Smt Bharti Dayal, <a href="/wiki/Mahasundari_Devi" title="Mahasundari Devi">Mahasundari Devi</a>, the late <a href="/wiki/Ganga_Devi_(painter)" title="Ganga Devi (painter)">Ganga Devi</a>, and Sita Devi.
</p><p>Mithila painting is also called <a href="/wiki/Madhubani_art" title="Madhubani art">Madhubani art</a>. It mostly depicts human beings and their association with nature.  Common scenes illustrate deities like <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rama" title="Rama">Ram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shiva" title="Shiva">Shiva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Durga" title="Durga">Durga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lakshmi" title="Lakshmi">Lakshmi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saraswati" title="Saraswati">Saraswati</a> from ancient epics. Natural objects like the sun, moon, and religious plants like <a href="/wiki/Tulsi" class="mw-redirect" title="Tulsi">Tulsi</a> are also widely painted, along with scenes from the royal court and social events like weddings. Generally, no space is left empty.<sup id="cite_ref-Carolyn_Brown_Heinz_2006,_pp._5-33_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carolyn_Brown_Heinz_2006,_pp._5-33-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Historically, the <a href="/wiki/Patna_School_of_Painting" title="Patna School of Painting">Patna School of Painting</a> (<i>Patna Salaam</i>), sometimes called <i>Company Painting</i>, flourished in Bihar during the early 18th to mid-20th centuries. The Patna School of Painting was an offshoot of the well-known <a href="/wiki/Mughal_painting" title="Mughal painting">Mughal</a> Miniature School of Painting. Those who practiced this art form were descendants of <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> artisans of Mughal painting. Facing persecution from the Mughal Emperor, <a href="/wiki/Aurangzeb" title="Aurangzeb">Aurangzeb</a>, these artisans found refuge, via <a href="/wiki/Murshidabad" title="Murshidabad">Murshidabad</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a> during the late 18th century. Their art shared the characteristics of the Mughal painters, but whereas the Mughal style depicted only royalty and court scenes, the <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a> artists also started painting <a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaar</a> scenes. They used <a href="/wiki/Watercolour" class="mw-redirect" title="Watercolour">watercolours</a> on paper and on <a href="/wiki/Mica" title="Mica">mica</a>. The style's subject matter evolved to include scenes of Indian daily life, local rulers, festivals, and ceremonies. This school of painting formed the basis for the formation of the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Arts_and_Crafts_Patna" class="mw-redirect" title="College of Arts and Crafts Patna">Patna Art School</a> under the leadership of Shri Radha Mohan. The school is an important center of the <a href="/wiki/Fine_arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Fine arts">fine arts</a> in Bihar.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bihar" title="Music of Bihar">Music of Bihar</a></div>
<p>Bihar has produced musicians like <a href="/wiki/Bharat_Ratna" title="Bharat Ratna">Bharat Ratna</a> <a href="/wiki/Ustad_Bismillah_Khan" class="mw-redirect" title="Ustad Bismillah Khan">Ustad Bismillah Khan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dhrupad" title="Dhrupad">dhrupad</a> singers like the Malliks (<a href="/wiki/Darbhanga_Gharana" title="Darbhanga Gharana">Darbhanga Gharana</a>) and the Mishras (<a href="/wiki/Bettiah" title="Bettiah">Bettiah</a> Gharana) along with poets like <a href="/wiki/Vidyapati" title="Vidyapati">Vidyapati</a> Thakur who contributed to <a href="/wiki/Maithili_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Maithili Music">Maithili Music</a>. The classical music in Bihar is a form of the <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_classical_music" title="Hindustani classical music">Hindustani classical music</a>.
<a href="/wiki/Gaya_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaya (India)">Gaya</a> is another centre of excellence in classical music, particularly of the <a href="/wiki/Tappa" title="Tappa">Tappa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thumri" title="Thumri">Thumri</a> varieties. <a href="/wiki/Pandit" title="Pandit">Pandit</a> Govardhan Mishra – son of the Ram Prasad Mishra, himself an accomplished singer – is perhaps the finest living exponent of Tappa singing in India today, according to <a href="/wiki/Padma_Shri" title="Padma Shri">Padma Shri</a> Gajendra Narayan Singh, founding secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Sangeet_Natak_Academi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sangeet Natak Academi">Sangeet Natak Academi</a> of Bihar. Gajendra Narayan Singh also writes, in his memoir, that Champanagar, <a href="/wiki/Banaili" title="Banaili">Banaili</a>, was another major centre of classical music. <a href="/wiki/Rajkumar_Shyamanand_Sinha" title="Rajkumar Shyamanand Sinha">Rajkumar Shyamanand Sinha</a> of Champanagar, Banaili princely state, was a great patron of music and was himself one of the finest exponents of classical vocal music in Bihar in his time.<sup id="cite_ref-Singh2008_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singh2008-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Singh, in another book on Indian classical music, has written that "Kumar Shyamanand Singh of Banaili estate had such expertise in singing that many great singers including <a href="/wiki/Kesarbai_Kerkar" title="Kesarbai Kerkar">Kesarbai Kerkar</a> acknowledged his ability. After listening to <a href="/wiki/Bandish" title="Bandish">bandishes</a> from Kumar Sahib, <a href="/wiki/Pandit_Jasraj" class="mw-redirect" title="Pandit Jasraj">Pandit Jasraj</a> was moved to tears and lamented that, alas, he did not have such ability himself." [free translation of Hindi text].<sup id="cite_ref-Singh1999_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singh1999-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SinghWeb_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SinghWeb-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 19th century, when the condition of Bihar worsened under the British misrule, many Biharis had to emigrate as indentured labourers to the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>. During this time many sad plays and songs called <i>birha</i> became popular, in the <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_region" title="Bhojpuri region">Bhojpur region</a>, thus <i>Bhojpuri Birha</i>. Dramas incorporating this theme continue to be popular in the theatres of <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jugnu2013_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jugnu2013-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (April 2016)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">

</p>
