<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Bihar" title="Cinema of Bihar">Cinema of Bihar</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_Film_Industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhojpuri Film Industry">Bhojpuri Film Industry</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bhojpuri_films" title="List of Bhojpuri films">List of Bhojpuri films</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anurita_Jha.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Anurita_Jha.jpg/180px-Anurita_Jha.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Anurita_Jha.jpg/270px-Anurita_Jha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Anurita_Jha.jpg/360px-Anurita_Jha.jpg 2x" data-file-width="585" data-file-height="881" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anurita_Jha.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Anurita_Jha" title="Anurita Jha">Anurita Jha</a> acted as the lead actress in Maithili film <a href="/wiki/Mithila_Makhaan" title="Mithila Makhaan">Mithila Makhaan</a></div></div></div>
<p>Bihar has a robust <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhojpuri">Bhojpuri</a>-language film industry. There is also a smaller production of <a href="/wiki/Magadhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Magadhi">Magadhi</a>-, <a href="/wiki/Maithili_language" title="Maithili language">Maithili</a>-, as well as <a href="/wiki/Angika" title="Angika">Angika</a>-language films. The first film with Bhojpuri dialogue was <i><a href="/wiki/Ganga_Jamuna" class="mw-redirect" title="Ganga Jamuna">Ganga Jamuna</a></i>, released in 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Bhaiyaa" title="Bhaiyaa">Bhaiyaa</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Magadhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Magadhi">Magadhi</a> film, was released in 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
The first <a href="/wiki/Maithili_language" title="Maithili language">Maithili</a> movie was <i><a href="/wiki/Kanyadan_film" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanyadan film">Kanyadan</a></i> released in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
Maithili film <a href="/wiki/Mithila_Makhaan" title="Mithila Makhaan">Mithila Makhaan</a> won the
<a href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards" title="National Film Awards">National Film Award</a> for Best Maithili Film in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
The history of films entirely in Bhojpuri begins in 1962 with the well-received film <i><a href="/wiki/Ganga_Maiyya_Tohe_Piyari_Chadhaibo" title="Ganga Maiyya Tohe Piyari Chadhaibo">Ganga Maiyya Tohe Piyari Chadhaibo</a></i> ("Mother Ganges, I will offer you a yellow sari"), which was directed by Kundan Kumar.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
1963's <i><a href="/wiki/Lagi_nahin_chute_ram" class="mw-redirect" title="Lagi nahin chute ram">Lagi nahin chute ram</a></i> was the all-time hit Bhojpuri film, and had higher attendance than <a href="/wiki/Mughal-e-Azam" title="Mughal-e-Azam">Mughal-e-Azam</a> in the eastern and northern regions of India. <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Nadiya_Ke_Paar_(1982_film)" title="Nadiya Ke Paar (1982 film)">Nadiya Ke Paar</a></i> is another of the most famous Bhojpuri-language movies. However, in the following years, films were produced only in fits and starts. Films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Bidesiya" title="Bidesiya">Bidesiya</a></i> ("Foreigner", 1963, directed by S. N. Tripathi) and <i><a href="/wiki/Ganga_(1965_film)" title="Ganga (1965 film)">Ganga</a></i> ("Ganges", 1965, directed by Kundan Kumar) were profitable and popular, but in general Bhojpuri films were not commonly produced in the 1960s and 1970s.
</p><p>In the 1980s, enough Bhojpuri films were produced to tentatively support a dedicated industry. Films such as <i>Mai</i> ("Mom", 1989, directed by Rajkumar Sharma) and <i>Hamar Bhauji</i> ("My Brother's Wife", 1983, directed by Kalpataru) continued to have at least sporadic success at the box office. However, this trend faded out by the end of the decade, and by 1990, the nascent industry seemed to be completely finished.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Bhojpuri film industry took off again in 2001 with the super hit <i>Saiyyan Hamar</i> ("My Sweetheart", directed by Mohan Prasad), which vaulted the hero of that film, <a href="/wiki/Ravi_Kishan" title="Ravi Kishan">Ravi Kishan</a>, to superstardom.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> This success was quickly followed by several other remarkably successful films, including <i>Panditji Batai Na Biyah Kab Hoi</i> ("Priest, tell me when I will marry", 2005, directed by Mohan Prasad) and <i>Sasura Bada Paisa Wala</i> ("My father-in-law, the rich guy", 2005). In a measure of the Bhojpuri film industry's rise, both of these did much better business in the states of Uttar Pradesh and Bihar than mainstream Bollywood hits at the time, and both films, made on extremely tight budgets, earned back more than ten times their production costs.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> <i>Sasura Bada Paisa Wala</i> also introduced <a href="/wiki/Manoj_Tiwari" title="Manoj Tiwari">Manoj Tiwari</a>, formerly a well-loved folk singer, to the wider audiences of <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_cinema" title="Bhojpuri cinema">Bhojpuri cinema</a>. The success of Ravi Kishan and Manoj Tiwari's films has led to a dramatic increase in Bhojpuri cinema's visibility, and the industry now supports an awards show<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> and a trade magazine, <i>Bhojpuri City</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> which chronicles the production and release of what are now over one hundred films per year.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Bihar" title="Religion in Bihar">Religion in Bihar</a></div>
<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">
&lt;div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;&lt;div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 3616.2362167392px; border-left-color:Green"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Green"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 52.465556445003px; border-left-color:Orange"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Orange"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Orange"></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religions in Bihar (2011)<sup id="cite_ref-census2011_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2011-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (82.69%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (16.87%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> (0.12%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Gray; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other religions (0.31%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> <a href="/wiki/Goddess" title="Goddess">Goddess</a> <a href="/wiki/Sita" title="Sita">Sita</a>, the consort of <a href="/wiki/Rama" title="Rama">Lord Rama</a> is believed to be born in <a href="/wiki/Sitamarhi_district" title="Sitamarhi district">Sitamarhi district</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mithila_(region)" title="Mithila (region)">Mithila region</a> of modern-day Bihar.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">Gautama Buddha</a> attained <a href="/wiki/Bodhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Bodhi">Enlightenment</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bodh_Gaya" title="Bodh Gaya">Bodh Gaya</a>, a town located in the modern day district of <a href="/wiki/Gaya_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaya District">Gaya</a> in Bihar. <a href="/wiki/Vasupujya" title="Vasupujya">Vasupujya</a>, the 12th Jain <a href="/wiki/Tirthankara" title="Tirthankara">Tirthankara</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Champapuri" title="Champapuri">Champapuri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhagalpur" title="Bhagalpur">Bhagalpur</a>. Vardhamana <a href="/wiki/Mahavira" title="Mahavira">Mahavira</a>, the 24th and the last <a href="/wiki/Tirthankara" title="Tirthankara">Tirthankara</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a>, was born in <a href="/wiki/Vaishali_(ancient_city)" title="Vaishali (ancient city)">Vaishali</a> around the 6th century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Bihar" title="Media in Bihar">Media in Bihar</a></div>
<p><i>Biharbandhu</i> was the first <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> newspaper published in Bihar. It was started in 1872 by Madan Mohan Bhatta, a <a href="/wiki/Marathi_people" title="Marathi people">Marathi</a> <a href="/wiki/Brahman" title="Brahman">Brahman</a> who settled in <a href="/wiki/Bihar-E-Sharif" class="mw-redirect" title="Bihar-E-Sharif">Bihar Sharif</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-journalism_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalism-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Hindi journalism in Bihar, and specially <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a>, could make little headway initially. Many Hindi journals were born and, after a lapse of time, vanished. Many journals were shelved even in the planning stages.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> But once Hindi had the support of being an official language, it started making inroads, even into the remote areas of Bihar. Hindi journalism acquired wisdom and maturity, and its longevity was assured. Hindi was introduced in the law courts in Bihar in 1880.<sup id="cite_ref-journalism_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalism-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Urdu journalism and poetry has a glorious past in Bihar. Many poets belong to Bihar, such as Shaad Azimabadi, Kaif Azimabadi, and Kalim Ajiz. Shanurahman, a world-famous radio announcer, is from Bihar. Many Urdu dailies— such as <i>Qomi Tanzim</i> and <i>Sahara</i>—are published in Bihar. There is a monthly Urdu magazine called <i>Voice of Bihar</i> – which is the first of its kind and is becoming popular among the Urdu speaking people.
</p><p>The beginning of the 20th century was marked by a number of notable new publications. A monthly magazine named <i>Bharat Ratna</i> was started in <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a>, in 1901. It was followed by <i>Ksahtriya Hitaishi</i>, <i>Aryavarta from Dinapure</i>, <i>Udyoga</i>, and <i>Chaitanya Chandrika</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> <i>Udyog</i> was edited by Vijyaanand Tripathy, a famous poet of the time, and <i>Chaitanya Chandrika</i> by Krishna Chaitanya Goswami, a literary figure of that time. The literary activity was not confined to <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a> alone but to other districts of Bihar.<sup id="cite_ref-journalism_139-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalism-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Dainik" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindustan Dainik">Hindustan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dainik_Jagran" title="Dainik Jagran">Dainik Jagran</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rajasthan_Patrika" title="Rajasthan Patrika">Rajasthan Patrika</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Aaj_(newspaper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aaj (newspaper)">Aaj</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Prabhat_Khabar" title="Prabhat Khabar">Prabhat Khabar</a></i> are some of the Hindi newspapers of Bihar. National English dailies like <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times_of_India" title="The Times of India">The Times of India</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Times" title="Hindustan Times">Hindustan Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Navbharat_Times" title="Navbharat Times">Navbharat Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Telegraph_(Kolkata)" title="The Telegraph (Kolkata)">The Telegraph</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economic_Times" title="The Economic Times">The Economic Times</a></i> have readers in the urban regions.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Bihar" title="Transport in Bihar">Transport in Bihar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Patna_river_port1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Patna_river_port1.JPG/220px-Patna_river_port1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Patna_river_port1.JPG/330px-Patna_river_port1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Patna_river_port1.JPG/440px-Patna_river_port1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="598" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Patna_river_port1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a> river port on national inland waterways-1 at Gai Ghat</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gai_Ghat_Patna.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Gai_Ghat_Patna.JPG/220px-Gai_Ghat_Patna.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Gai_Ghat_Patna.JPG/330px-Gai_Ghat_Patna.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Gai_Ghat_Patna.JPG/440px-Gai_Ghat_Patna.JPG 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="598" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gai_Ghat_Patna.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Steamboat" title="Steamboat">Steamers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dredger" class="mw-redirect" title="Dredger">dredgers</a> at Gai Ghat, <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airways">Airways</span></h3>
<p>Bihar has two operational airports: <a href="/wiki/Lok_Nayak_Jayaprakash_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Lok Nayak Jayaprakash Airport">Lok Nayak Jayaprakash Airport</a>, Patna; and <a href="/wiki/Gaya_Airport" title="Gaya Airport">Gaya Airport</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inland_Waterways">Inland Waterways</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ganges" title="Ganges">Ganges</a> – navigable throughout the year – was the principal river highway across the vast north <a href="/wiki/Indo-Gangetic_Plain" title="Indo-Gangetic Plain">Indo-Gangetic Plain</a>. Vessels capable of accommodating five hundred merchants were known to ply this river in the ancient period; it served as a conduit for overseas trade, as goods were carried from <a href="/wiki/Pataliputra" title="Pataliputra">Pataliputra</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a>) and Champa (later <a href="/wiki/Bhagalpur" title="Bhagalpur">Bhagalpur</a>) out to the seas and to ports in <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> and Southeast Asia. The role of the Ganges as a channel for trade was enhanced by its natural links – it embraces all the major rivers and streams in both north and south Bihar.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Bihar" title="Tourism in Bihar">Tourism in Bihar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mahabodhitemple.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Mahabodhitemple.jpg/200px-Mahabodhitemple.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Mahabodhitemple.jpg/300px-Mahabodhitemple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Mahabodhitemple.jpg/400px-Mahabodhitemple.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mahabodhitemple.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Mahabodhi_Temple" title="Mahabodhi Temple">Mahabodhi Temple</a>, among the four holy sites related to the life of the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Buddha" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Buddha">Lord Buddha</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a></div></div></div>
<p>The culture and heritage of Bihar can be observed from the large number of <a href="/wiki/Ancient" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient">ancient</a> <a href="/wiki/Monument" title="Monument">monuments</a> spread throughout the state. Bihar is visited by many tourists from around the world,<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> with about 24,000,000 (24 <a href="/wiki/Million" class="mw-redirect" title="Million">million</a>) tourists visiting the state each year.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In earlier days, tourism in the region was purely based on <a href="/wiki/Educational_tourism" class="mw-redirect" title="Educational tourism">educational tourism</a>, as Bihar was home of some prominent ancient universities like <a href="/wiki/Nalanda" title="Nalanda">Nalanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vikramashila" title="Vikramashila">Vikramashila</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:30px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barabar_Nagarjuni_Caves,_Anantavarman_Inscription_Sanskrit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Barabar_Nagarjuni_Caves%2C_Anantavarman_Inscription_Sanskrit.jpg/120px-Barabar_Nagarjuni_Caves%2C_Anantavarman_Inscription_Sanskrit.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Barabar_Nagarjuni_Caves%2C_Anantavarman_Inscription_Sanskrit.jpg/180px-Barabar_Nagarjuni_Caves%2C_Anantavarman_Inscription_Sanskrit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Barabar_Nagarjuni_Caves%2C_Anantavarman_Inscription_Sanskrit.jpg/240px-Barabar_Nagarjuni_Caves%2C_Anantavarman_Inscription_Sanskrit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a></div></div>

<p>Barabar Caves – Asokan Inscription
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">

</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Bihar" title="Education in Bihar">Education in Bihar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Literacy_in_Bihar" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy in Bihar">Literacy in Bihar</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_educational_institutions_in_Bihar" class="mw-redirect" title="List of educational institutions in Bihar">List of educational institutions in Bihar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Front_view_of_administrative_building_of_IIT_Patna.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Front_view_of_administrative_building_of_IIT_Patna.jpg/220px-Front_view_of_administrative_building_of_IIT_Patna.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Front_view_of_administrative_building_of_IIT_Patna.jpg/330px-Front_view_of_administrative_building_of_IIT_Patna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Front_view_of_administrative_building_of_IIT_Patna.jpg/440px-Front_view_of_administrative_building_of_IIT_Patna.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4800" data-file-height="2400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Front_view_of_administrative_building_of_IIT_Patna.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Front view of administrative building of IIT Patna</div></div></div>
<p>Historically, Bihar has been a major centre of learning, home to the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Universities_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Universities of India">ancient universities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nalanda" title="Nalanda">Nalanda</a> <small>(established in 450 CE)</small>, <a href="/wiki/Jagaddala" class="mw-redirect" title="Jagaddala">Odantapurā</a> <small>(established in 550CE)</small> and <a href="/wiki/Vikramashila" title="Vikramashila">Vikramashila</a> <small>(established in 783 CE)</small>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> This tradition of learning may have been stultified during the period of Turkic invasions, c. 1000 CE, at which point it is believed major education centers, maintained by reclusive communities of Buddhist monks removed from the local populace, were suppressed by the Turkic raids originating from central Asia .<sup id="cite_ref-Scott_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bihar saw a revival of its education system during the later part of the <a href="/wiki/British_raj" class="mw-redirect" title="British raj">British rule</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Patna_University" title="Patna University">Patna University</a>, the seventh oldest university of the Indian subcontinent, was established in 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Some other centres of high learning established under British rule are <a href="/wiki/Patna_College" title="Patna College">Patna College</a> (established 1839), Bihar School of Engineering (1900; now known as <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Technology,_Patna" title="National Institute of Technology, Patna">National Institute of Technology, Patna</a>), Prince of Wales Medical College (1925; now <a href="/wiki/Patna_Medical_College_and_Hospital" title="Patna Medical College and Hospital">Patna Medical College and Hospital</a>), <a href="/wiki/Science_College,_Patna" class="mw-redirect" title="Science College, Patna">Science College, Patna</a> (1928), <a href="/wiki/Patna_Women%27s_College" title="Patna Women&#39;s College">Patna Women's College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bihar_Veterinary_College" title="Bihar Veterinary College">Bihar Veterinary College</a> (established 1927), Imperial Agriculture Research Institute (1905; now <a href="/wiki/Dr._Rajendra_Prasad_Central_Agriculture_University" title="Dr. Rajendra Prasad Central Agriculture University">Dr. Rajendra Prasad Central Agriculture University, Pusa</a>) among others.
</p><p>A recent survey by <a href="/wiki/Pratham" title="Pratham">Pratham</a> rated the receptivity of Bihari children to their teaching as being better than those in other states.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Bihar is striving to increase female literacy, now at 53.3%, as the government establishes educational institutions. At the time of independence, women's literacy in Bihar was 4.22%.
</p>
<table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin-left:.6em;" align="right">

<p>In 1964 <a href="/wiki/Bihar_School_of_Yoga" title="Bihar School of Yoga">Bihar School of Yoga</a> was established at <a href="/wiki/Munger" title="Munger">Munger</a>.
</p><p>Bihar has a <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Technology" title="National Institutes of Technology">National Institute of Technology (NIT)</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institutes_of_Technology" title="Indian Institutes of Technology">Indian Institute of Technology (IIT)</a> in Patna. The National Employability Report of Engineering Graduates, 2014<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> puts graduates from Bihar in the top 25 percent of the country, and rating Bihar as one of the three top states at producing engineering graduates in terms of quality and employability.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of December 2013, there are seven government engineering colleges in the public sector, and 12 engineering colleges in the private sector, in Bihar, besides government-aided <a href="/wiki/BIT_Patna" class="mw-redirect" title="BIT Patna">BIT Patna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Institute_of_Technology" title="Women&#39;s Institute of Technology">Women's Institute of Technology</a>, Darbhanga. The overall annual intake of students of these technical institutes in Bihar is only 6,200.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Bihar, government colleges are located at Muzaffarpur, Bhagalpur, Gaya, Darbhanga, Motihari, Nalanda, and Saran (Chhapra). All institutes are recognised by <a href="/wiki/All_India_Council_for_Technical_Education" title="All India Council for Technical Education">All India Council for Technical Education</a> (AICTE), affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Aryabhatta_Knowledge_University" title="Aryabhatta Knowledge University">Aryabhatta Knowledge University</a> (AKU). As it is, the foundation stone of the eighth engineering college of the state government, Ramdhari Singh Dinkar Engineering College, was laid on 22 December 2013 at <a href="/wiki/Begusarai" title="Begusarai">Begusarai</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> while the process of creating the infrastructure for two new engineering colleges – one each at <a href="/wiki/Madhepura" title="Madhepura">Madhepura</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sitamarhi" title="Sitamarhi">Sitamarhi</a> – has started.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NITPMainBuilding.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/NITPMainBuilding.jpg/220px-NITPMainBuilding.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/NITPMainBuilding.jpg/330px-NITPMainBuilding.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/NITPMainBuilding.jpg/440px-NITPMainBuilding.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1023" data-file-height="750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NITPMainBuilding.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NIT Patna main building</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Technology,_Patna" title="National Institute of Technology, Patna">NIT Patna</a> is the second oldest <a href="/wiki/Engineering_college" class="mw-redirect" title="Engineering college">engineering college</a> of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. Its origin can be traced to 1886, with the establishment of a survey training school, subsequently renamed Bihar College of Engineering in 1932. In 2004, the government of India upgraded the college to <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="National Institute of Technology">National Institute of Technology</a> (NIT) status. In 2007, NIT Patna was granted <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_National_Importance" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of National Importance">Institute of National Importance</a> status, in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Technology_Act,_2007" title="National Institutes of Technology Act, 2007">National Institutes of Technology Act, 2007</a>.
</p><p>Bihar established several new educational institutes between 2006 and 2008. <a href="/wiki/Birla_Institute_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Birla Institute of Technology">BIT Mesra</a> started its <a href="/wiki/BIT_Patna" class="mw-redirect" title="BIT Patna">Patna extension centre</a> in September 2006. On 8 August 2008, <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institutes_of_Technology_Patna" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Institutes of Technology Patna">Indian Institutes of Technology Patna</a> was inaugurated with students from all over India<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhas_Institute_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Netaji Subhas Institute of Technology">NSIT</a> opened its new college in <a href="/wiki/Bihta" title="Bihta">Bihta</a>, which is now emerging as an education hub.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bhagalpur_College_of_Engineering" title="Bhagalpur College of Engineering">BCE, Bhagalpur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muzaffarpur_Institute_of_Technology" title="Muzaffarpur Institute of Technology">MIT, Muzaffarpur</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Pharmaceutical_Education_and_Research,_Hajipur" title="National Institute of Pharmaceutical Education and Research, Hajipur">National Institute of Pharmaceutical Education and Research, Hajipur</a> (NIPER)<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> are in Bihar. On 4 August 2008, <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Fashion_Technology_Patna" class="mw-redirect" title="National Institute of Fashion Technology Patna">National Institute of Fashion Technology Patna</a> was established as the ninth such institute in India.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chanakya_National_Law_University" title="Chanakya National Law University">Chanakya National Law University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chandragupt_Institute_of_Management" title="Chandragupt Institute of Management">Chandragupt Institute of Management</a> were established in the later half of 2008. Steps are being taken to revive the ancient Nalanda Mahavihara as Nalanda International University. Countries such as Japan, Korea, and China have also taken initiatives. The A.N. Sinha Institute<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> of Social Studies is a premier research institute in the state.
</p><p>Bihar e-Governance Services &amp; Technologies (BeST) and the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Bihar" title="Government of Bihar">government of Bihar</a> have initiated a unique program to establish a centre of excellence called <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bihar_Knowledge_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bihar Knowledge Center (page does not exist)">Bihar Knowledge Center</a>, a finishing school to equip students with the latest skills and customised short-term training programs at an affordable cost. The centre aims to attract the youth of the state to improve their technical, professional, and soft skills, to meet the current requirements of the industrial job market.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bihar has the <a href="/wiki/Central_Institute_of_Plastics_Engineering_%26_Technology,_Hajipur" title="Central Institute of Plastics Engineering &amp; Technology, Hajipur">Central Institute of Plastic Engineering &amp; Technology</a> (CIPET) and the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Hotel_Management,_Hajipur" title="Institute of Hotel Management, Hajipur">Institute of Hotel Management</a> (a central government unit) in <a href="/wiki/Hajipur" title="Hajipur">Hajipur</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_University_of_Bihar" class="mw-redirect" title="Central University of Bihar">Central University of Bihar</a> (CUB) is one of the sixteen <a href="/wiki/Central_universities_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Central universities (India)">central universities</a> newly established by the Government of India under the Central Universities Act, 2009 (Section 25 of 2009). The university is temporarily located on the premises of the Birla Institute of Technology, Patna. The university is likely to be relocated to Panchanpur, approximately 10 kilometres (6.2&#160;mi) from Gaya, on 300 acres (120&#160;ha) of land to be transferred soon from the military. On 28 February 2014, Lok Sabha Speaker Meira Kumar laid the foundation stone.
</p><p>In 2010 Government of Bihar established <a href="/wiki/Bihar_Agricultural_University" title="Bihar Agricultural University">Bihar Agricultural University</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sabour" title="Sabour">Sabour</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bhagalpur" title="Bhagalpur">Bhagalpur</a> district. It has ten colleges.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi_Central_University" title="Mahatma Gandhi Central University">Mahatma Gandhi Central University</a>—also established under the Central Universities Act, and Amendment Act of 2014—is situated in <a href="/wiki/Motihari" title="Motihari">Motihari</a>, the district headquarters of East Champaran district.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/All_India_Institute_of_Medical_Sciences,_Patna" title="All India Institute of Medical Sciences, Patna">All India Institute of Medical Sciences, Patna</a> was established in 2012.
</p><p>On 3 July 2013, chief minister <a href="/wiki/Nitish_Kumar" title="Nitish Kumar">Nitish Kumar</a> laid foundation stone for a new campus of <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Electronics_%26_Information_Technology" title="National Institute of Electronics &amp; Information Technology">National Institute of Electronics &amp; Information Technology</a> in Amara cillage, near <a href="/wiki/Bihta" title="Bihta">Bihta</a> township.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> It was inaugurated in February 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
Bihar has eight Bihar Government funded medical colleges.
</p><p>Bihar has eight Government funded medical colleges namely <a href="/wiki/Patna_Medical_College_and_Hospital" title="Patna Medical College and Hospital">Patna Medical College and Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nalanda_Medical_College_and_Hospital" title="Nalanda Medical College and Hospital">Nalanda Medical College and Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vardhman_Institute_of_Medical_Sciences" title="Vardhman Institute of Medical Sciences">Vardhman Institute of Medical Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_Institute_of_Medical_Sciences" title="Indira Gandhi Institute of Medical Sciences">Indira Gandhi Institute of Medical Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darbhanga_Medical_College_and_Hospital" title="Darbhanga Medical College and Hospital">Darbhanga Medical College and Hospital</a>, Anugarh Narayan Magadh Medical College and Hospital Gaya, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Krishna_Medical_College_and_Hospital" title="Sri Krishna Medical College and Hospital">Sri Krishna Medical College and Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_Medical_College,_Bhagalpur" title="Jawaharlal Nehru Medical College, Bhagalpur">Jawaharlal Nehru Medical College, Bhagalpur</a>, Government Medical College, Bettiah and five private medical colleges<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2019, deputy chief minister <a href="/wiki/Sushil_Modi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sushil Modi">Sushil Modi</a> announced the Bihar government's planned to establish 11 new medical colleges at Chhapra, Purnia, Samastipur, Bengusarai, Sitamarhi, Vaishali, Jhanjharpur, Siwan, Buxar, Bhojpur, Jamui and a dental college at Rahui in Nalanda district is under construction. There are also plans on constructing a cancer institute within <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_Institute_of_Medical_Sciences" title="Indira Gandhi Institute of Medical Sciences">Indira Gandhi Institute of Medical Sciences</a> premises and transformation of <a href="/wiki/Patna_Medical_College_and_Hospital" title="Patna Medical College and Hospital">Patna Medical College and Hospital</a> into a world class health centre.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014 the government of Bihar established <a href="/wiki/Development_Management_Institute" title="Development Management Institute">Development Management Institute</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bihta" title="Bihta">Bihta</a> near the <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nalanda_University" title="Nalanda University">Nalanda University</a> was re-established in 2014.
</p><p>In 2015, the central government had proposed reestablishment of <a href="/wiki/Vikramshila" class="mw-redirect" title="Vikramshila">Vikramshila</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bhagalpur" title="Bhagalpur">Bhagalpur</a> and had designated <span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span> 500crores for it.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Management_Bodh_Gaya" title="Indian Institute of Management Bodh Gaya">Indian Institute of Management Bodh Gaya</a> was established in 2015.
</p><p>In 2016 the government of Bihar established <a href="/wiki/Patliputra_University" title="Patliputra University">Patliputra University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munger_University" title="Munger University">Munger University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Purnea_University" title="Purnea University">Purnea University</a> through Bihar state university bill.
</p><p>Government of Bihar established Bihar Animal Science University in 2017. It has three constituent colleges namely, <a href="/wiki/Bihar_Veterinary_College" title="Bihar Veterinary College">Bihar Veterinary College</a>, Sanjay Gandhi Institute of Diary Technology (Patna) and College of Fisheries, Kishanganj.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Information_Technology,_Bhagalpur" title="Indian Institute of Information Technology, Bhagalpur">Indian Institute of Information Technology, Bhagalpur</a>, was established in 2017.
</p><p>In March 2019, the government of Bihar has sent a proposal to centre Government to upgrade <a href="/wiki/Darbhanga_Medical_College_and_Hospital" title="Darbhanga Medical College and Hospital">Darbhanga Medical College and Hospital</a> into an <a href="/wiki/AIIMS" class="mw-redirect" title="AIIMS">AIIMS</a>-like institution.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-Cardona2003-118"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Cardona2003_118-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/George_Cardona" title="George Cardona">Cardona, George</a>; Jain, Dhanesh, eds.
